Spring and Autumn

Odds and Ends

— (Yang Yusheng)

"Zhi Zhui" (置喙) is a "Phrase" commonly used by Japanese diplomats. In colloquial Chinese, it is similar in meaning to "cha zui" (挿嘴), which means "to interject."

As a rule, you won't hear "Yes" or "No" from the mouths of diplomats! Because their phrasing is focused on being tactful. But Japanese diplomats are much more straightforward. When using the "Zhi Zhui" phrase, it is often linked to the words "Bu Rong" (不容), meaning "do not allow." This is a warning to the other party, saying "don't butt in!" It has the same meaning as the English "Shut Up," but without the same "angry" tone!

The day before yesterday, I saw three or four hooligans beating a "bumpkin" on the street. Among the silent bystanders, someone actually came forward to defend him! The hooligans glared at him and told him to "scram!" They had an air of "no interjection allowed!"

This made me think about why God created humans with two ears, two eyes, two hands, and two feet, but only one mouth! Humans shouldn't be so talkative!

Streamlined

— Wei Jing

Curves, apart from the contours of women's beautiful bodies, have long been overlooked. Three-dimensionality is also gradually being forgotten by the general public. It is said that "streamlined" is the style of 1935.

Therefore, airplanes, trains, and motorcycles of 1935 are all streamlined. Naturally, this is very reasonable, because streamlined designs reduce the risk of damage in storms, and in good weather, they can reduce the resistance of air pressure and increase the speed of forward movement.

I realized that the buildings of this year may gradually become streamlined. The yurts in the desert, the coconut and palm leaf huts in the hot zones, and the Chinese tomb-style houses may become good models for the 1935-style buildings.

Naturally, this is not limited to buildings. Even furniture and utensils, this year, I think, clever designers will transform from three-dimensional to without corners, but not the multi-curved style that was popular before, to create the 1935-style streamlined designs for modern families to purchase.

Look, the window displays in large stores are not showing much three-dimensionality this year. Even whole bolts of silk cloth are displayed using streamlined methods to attract passersby to stop and watch.

In the material realm, there is streamlining. In the spiritual realm, I think, this year may also become increasingly streamlined. The three-dimensional, upright, and honest character is not popular anymore. Those who speak and act without corners that might bump into people, or corners that people can grab, can be considered streamlined, and are the non-outdated forerunners of the times.

The Fragrant and Beautiful Wanli Bridge

— A Rustic Old Man

I recently read Mr. Lu Jia's "Wanli Bridge" in this column, which said that the bridge is located in Shangcheng County, Henan, built with stone blocks, and is eighteen miles long. There are four small teahouses on the bridge for travelers to rest their feet, which shows how long the bridge is. Only small sheep-horn carts can be used for transportation on the bridge. Mr. Lu Jia did not mention any other famous scenic spots or romantic tales.

I remember Hu Zeng's poem to Xue Tao, the famous courtesan of the Tang Dynasty: "The lady calligrapher is by Wanli Bridge, living in seclusion beneath the loquat blossoms; How many talented men have come to woo, yet none can match the spring breeze." Xue Tao was a famous courtesan in Sichuan, and her fragrant boudoir was clearly built by Wanli Bridge. So, this Wanli Bridge is certainly not in Henan. For example, Luoyang Bridge is not in Luoyang, Henan, but in Huian, Fujian. Tianjin Bridge is not in Tianjin, Hebei, but in Luoyang, Henan. A place becomes famous because of its people. The Wanli Bridge in Sichuan is certainly more famous than the one in Henan.

According to research, the Wanli Bridge in Sichuan is located south of Huayang County. The Gazeteer of Famous Sites says: "The Shu envoy Fei Wei was sent to Wu, and Zhuge Liang saw him off. Wei happily said: 'The journey of ten thousand miles begins today,' hence the name." It can be seen that this Wanli Bridge was not named because of its length.

The thatched cottage of the Tang Dynasty poet Du Fu was west of Wanli Bridge. Du Fu's poem contains the line "A thatched cottage west of Wanli Bridge." The famous Tang Dynasty courtesan Xue Tao also lived by Wanli Bridge, hence Hu Zeng's line "The lady calligrapher is by Wanli Bridge."

Flying Kites

— Master of Spring Rain Tower

In the spring season, there is no more suitable exercise than flying kites. However, flying kites is not just a pastime for children; many adults also enjoy it. It is almost universally popular in the Jiangnan area, especially in Changzhou and Wuxi, where even more people love it.

Last spring, I took the Shanghai-Nanjing train from Nanjing to Suzhou. Passing through Changzhou and Wuxi, I saw through the train window, in the inky black wilderness and dark sky, kite lanterns flickering like long snakes. Isn't that an interesting thing for adults to do?

During the day, when we go for a walk in the countryside, we often hear a faint and melodious sound carried by the gentle spring breeze. This is clearly the sound of a zheng (stringed instrument) attached to the kite; otherwise, there would be no such sound waves in the clear sky. At this time, taking a spring outing in the countryside with a kindred spirit, stepping on the soft green grass, with the warm spring sunshine shining on us, we might as well sing a "Spring Song" to complement the intoxicating spring scenery.

The day before yesterday, I received a letter from a friend in Changzhou, inviting me to a kite flying competition. I used thatch as the frame and red silk as the skin to make a very exquisite star kite. With a thin silk thread, I will let it fly freely and surely win praise. Soon, I want to take it to the competition. But we in Si'an are also having a kite flying competition, scheduled for March 16th. Friends who love kites will certainly bring all kinds of different kites to participate, and the sky will be adorned with great beauty!

Arbor Day

Small Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Jia Duocai smiled and said, "I understand what you mean even if you don't say it. It's probably that besides accompanying people to smoke and play cards, there are some other things. Then you should have earned some money, why are you so poor as to do this kind of thing?" Yang Wanhua said, "Alas! It's really my own fault. Because I accompanied people to smoke, I could smoke for free, and I became addicted without realizing it. Originally, I felt very uncomfortable, and smiling and talking to people was forced. These days are even more difficult than being beaten and scolded. By last autumn, I had developed all kinds of hidden illnesses, and my face was even uglier after being smoked by the cigarettes. Within a month, it was difficult to find someone who was willing to buy my body. For example, last time, Mr. Li introduced me to Mr. Jia, and I tried my best to please him, but Mr. Jia didn't want me. Isn't that clear proof? Today, someone opened a room next door and called me over. He didn't like me, smoked with me for a while, and left first. I thought the room fee was already paid, so I might as well sleep here for one night and wait for another opportunity. Unexpectedly, I accidentally saw your banknotes in the crack of the wall. It doesn't matter if I don't have food or cigarettes, but I have a chest pain problem that occurs every three or four days, and I can't bear it. I rented a room in the southern alley from the local people, because it saves some money, but it is too inconvenient, and I have to do everything myself. When my illness flares up, who will take care of me? I can only wait to die. Moreover, the landlords don't want to rent to me anymore. I really want to find some money to treat my illness, and it would be even better if I could find more money to escape back to Henan. When I saw the money you put on the table in the crack of the wall, it was enough for me to spend my way home. If I became a thief once and stole this money to go home and reform, wouldn't that be a good plan? I know you don't care about this little bit of money, so I took action. If it were a poor person, I wouldn't dare to touch it. However, I'm always sorry to you, sir. I'm willing to do whatever you want me to do. I only have this body left, sir!" As she spoke, she sobbed again. (163)

Imperial Incense Misty Record

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

"Now is the time for silkworms to spin silk and build their cocoons!" One morning, the Empress Dowager thought of the spring silkworms she kept and led us to visit them again. While Her Old Majesty was talking to us eloquently, the girls raising silkworms were busy working! They are indeed very busy these days; but for the rest of the year, they can eat their fill and do nothing, sleeping in the garden. "We are different here from the outside world! Ordinary people mostly tie dry firewood into short bundles and put the silkworms that are about to spin silk on them, letting them make cocoons there; the silk obtained in this way is often not very smooth. So, we use specially made small boxes, each box containing four silkworms." The Empress Dowager pointed to the many paper boxes stacked high over there and continued to say to me: "After they go in, they will each occupy a corner and make cocoons without interfering with each other. You can come and see often if you don't believe me!"

I really obeyed her words and came to see them even more often. It was indeed very interesting! Whenever a silkworm is about to spin silk, it no longer eats mulberry leaves, as if it is already too full; at this time, its body is very thick and long, and it has become a transparent color. So, the girls raising silkworms gently put them into those small boxes, four in each box, covered the box and placed it flat, letting them work hard to make cocoons. After about five or six days, when the box is opened, four white or golden cocoons have been neatly formed in the four corners of the box. However, it is said that the four silkworms in a box must be of the same color. If three are white and one is yellow, the yellow one will not spin any further after completing half of its cocoon; so, they must be distinguished in advance and not mixed up. (274)

Shortcut

— Yu Sheng

In the evening, go to the bathhouse, undress, and take a bath. After bathing, dress and go home, then undress again and go to bed. Why not just have a car carry you directly to your bed after bathing!

In the yarn factory, cotton is ginned, spun into yarn, reeled, packaged, and sold. The weaving factory, however, unpacks the bales, applies sizing, and puts the yarn on the looms. Why not sell the reeled yarn directly to the weaving factory!

These are just jokes, but Chinese people really take too many detours when doing things! They are unwilling to take shortcuts, so they are always falling behind!

Travels

Cherry Blossoms on Three Islands

— Xunzi

The waves of the southeast wind bring news of spring. Spring is truly a season for outings. The plum blossoms of Dengwei and the peach blossoms of Longhua, one after another, smile and offer themselves for people to enjoy. Even more so, the cherry blossoms of Three Islands bloom a little later than the plum blossoms and a little earlier than the peach blossoms, making visitors linger and reluctant to leave!

The cherry blossom is the national flower of Japan. Whenever the season of full bloom arrives, the whole country is truly in a frenzy. Factories and schools all take holidays, and even the police wear paper cherry blossoms on their hats. On the streets, people walk as if writing calligraphy with their feet, humming songs with a humming sound in their mouths – these are the drunkards returning from viewing the cherry blossoms. Viewing flowers must involve drinking. In ancient China, there was Shan Tao, who "would not return home unless drunk." In Japan, during the cherry blossom season, temporary sake shops are set up everywhere with reed mats. The workers will exchange the money they have accumulated from a month of hard work for sake and get drunk under the cherry blossom trees. The workers in Japan understand "the art of life" better than those outside Japan.

In the late second month, when the "lingering cold has not yet faded," people sitting on mats still feel a bit of pain in their fingertips and have to reach out to warm them over a large pot. However, newspapers such as the Asahi Shimbun and the Mainichi Shimbun are already urging readers in a slow and gentle tone, saying that "the season of flowers is about to arrive." Because the cherry blossom is the national flower of Japan, the single word "flower" can represent cherry blossoms on Three Islands. Occasionally, when an early-blooming cherry blossom in Ueno Park puts out two or three buds on its branches before his companions can feel the "grace of spring," it causes a big stir! The photographers from the newspapers, with you carrying a camera and me carrying a tripod, rush to Ueno to photograph the buds. A little later, the morning or evening newspaper prints the photos, and people, seeing the report, run to Ueno to "find it according to the picture."

Besides the cherry blossoms of Ueno Park, Mount Asukayama is also a famous place for viewing cherry blossoms in Tokyo. Mount Asukayama is located outside Tokyo and can be reached by train in an instant. The mountain is not very high, about the same as Tiger Hill in Suzhou. Besides cherry blossoms, there is nothing else to play. However, the Japanese have great skill in embellishing natural scenery. They plant cherry blossoms all over the mountains and fields, so that visitors walk under the cherry blossom trees from the foot of the mountain to the top. At the end of each section of the road, there are temporary sake shops, tea shops, cafes, and restaurants covered with reed mats. Visitors not only wear colorful floral clothes to fulfill "dressing in brocade and walking in the daytime," but also have strangely dressed men and women with makeup like in old Chinese dramas, with painted faces, and some wearing masks. Everyone puts the two words "carnival" into practice.

Sports News

The Long-Suspended Sino-Portuguese Football Cup Will Be Revived, To Be Held After the World Cup

The Sino-Portuguese football match, which has been suspended for many years, was initially sponsored with a large silver cup donated by the Portuguese Sports Association. The two teams hold three matches each year in a best-of-three system, with the annual winner determined within three years. The team that wins two years out of the three will have permanent possession of the cup. China won the first edition, but the second was never completed. Afterwards, either due to time constraints or the incomplete Portuguese team, it could not continue. There was a proposal to revive it last year, but it did not materialize due to time constraints. This year, the football association feels very relaxed, and with the Portuguese having a lot of talent and winning the World Cup final, the enthusiasm is very good. Therefore, both the Chinese and Portuguese sides are actively working to continue the event. According to a staff member of the National Sports Association, the competition will be held after the World Cup.

A Chinese Innovation: Indoor Lawn Tennis at Shen Garden on Sunday Evening: Zheng Zhaojia vs. Carlson

Zheng Zhaojia, who was selected to represent China in lawn tennis and went to the Philippines for training, arrived in Shanghai last week by boat with Mrs. Dimitri Vreede. According to Mrs. Vreede, whose original name is Helen Marlowe, she was the All-American Women's Champion in 1930 and is currently ranked 15th in the United States. Yesterday, she practiced at Shen Garden with Zheng, Carlson, and others. Her various strokes and postures were perfect, truly living up to her reputation. Now that the Shanghai Basketball League has ended, the authorities are using this venue to plan indoor lawn tennis to provide practice for Xu and Zheng before they go abroad. It was set up a few days ago. Indoor lawn tennis, which requires playing under lights, is still a novelty in China. It has been agreed that Mrs. Vreede, Carlson, Zheng Zhaojia, and Jia Bude will hold a singles and doubles exhibition match on Sunday evening (the 24th) of this week for the appreciation of the people of Shanghai. The order of the two matches is set as follows:

Overview of Kindergartens in Provinces and Cities in the 20th Year of the Republic

The Ministry of Education has compiled statistics on the status of kindergartens in various provinces and cities in the 20th year of the Republic. The following is a summary:

(1) Number of Kindergartens: In the 20th year of the Republic, there were a total of 829 public and private kindergartens in various provinces and cities across the country, with Sichuan having the most at 164, followed by Fujian at 79, Jiangsu at 78, Zhejiang at 69, Guangdong at 59, Shaanxi at 51, Shanghai at 40, Anhui at 36, Henan at 26, Shandong and Hebei at 24 each, Nanjing at 23, Hebei at 21, Yunnan at 20, Hubei at 19, Shanxi at 14, Beiping at 12, Jiangxi at 11, Xikang at 10, Gansu at 8, Guangxi at 6, Guizhou and Qingdao at 5 each, Qinghai at 2, and Chahar at 1.

(2) Number of Students: There were a total of 36,770 kindergarten students nationwide. Public Training Exhibition to Open on the 28th

Schools Allowed Half-Day Off for Visit; Education Bureau Notifies

The Shanghai Education Bureau instructed municipal and registered private primary and secondary schools, stating that the Shanghai Civic Training Exhibition is scheduled to open at 9:00 AM on March 28th. All schools should send representatives to the opening ceremony. The number of representatives from each school is determined based on the school's situation and distance as follows: (A) Each normal school, vocational school, and middle school should send at least four teachers and staff representatives and ten student representatives; (B) Each elementary school in the South Shanghai district should send at least two teachers and staff representatives and four student representatives; (C) Each elementary school in the North Shanghai district should send at least two teachers and staff representatives and two student representatives; (D) Each elementary school in the rural district should send at least one teacher and staff representative and two student representatives. Furthermore, during the exhibition period, except for the holiday on the 29th to commemorate the martyrs, when schools are free to visit, schools may have a half-day off to visit the exhibition on the other two days. The visiting dates for each school are as follows: March 28th, normal schools, vocational schools, and elementary schools in the South Shanghai district; March 29th, all schools are free to visit; March 30th, middle schools and elementary schools in the North Shanghai and rural districts. Also, all schools exhibiting items must assign staff to be responsible for the arrangement, safekeeping, and retrieval of exhibits from the start to the end of the exhibition. During the exhibition, they should provide detailed explanations to visitors' inquiries. Staff members on duty each day must wear school badges for identification. All the above points are hereby urgently ordered to be followed by the respective schools.

Zhang Yousan and He Bingsong Explain the Meaning of Indigenous Chinese Culture

Since the publication of the Ten Professors' Declaration, it has aroused national discussion, and the enthusiasm has been advancing with the times. However, the general public's understanding of the meaning of culture and indigenous Chinese culture is quite inconsistent. At the same time, some believe that the proposition of the Ten Professors' Declaration is exactly the same as the proposition of "Chinese learning as the foundation, Western learning for practical application." Therefore, the signatories of the Ten Professors' Declaration, whenever invited to speak on cultural construction issues, make efforts to explain the definition of culture and the similarities and differences between the indigenous Chinese culture and the proposition of Chinese learning as the foundation and Western learning for practical application, hoping that the general public can also gain a practical understanding. The key points of the speeches by Zhang Yousan and He Bingsong at Guanghua University and the Chinese Vocational Education Society are excerpted below to inform those who are interested in the cultural construction movement.

Zhang Yousan's View on Indigenous Chinese Culture: Mr. Zhang Yi was invited to give a public lecture at Guanghua University yesterday, with the topic being "Is 'Chinese Learning as the Foundation and Western Learning for Practical Application' Correct?" He elaborated on the inadequacy of this proposition in integrating Chinese and Western cultures. Mr. Zhang's lecture mainly stated that the adoption of both Chinese and Western cultures can be divided into two types: mixture and synthesis. Chinese learning as the foundation and Western learning for practical application is only a mixture, while what is needed is synthesis. Moreover, the synthesis process must be prepared in advance and cannot be allowed to proceed arbitrarily. Specifically, it is necessary to adopt both the spirit of self-discipline in Chinese culture and the science of the West to create a new Chinese culture.

He Bingsong's Speech at the Vocational Education Society: The Chinese Vocational Education Society specially invited Mr. He Bingsong, a signatory of the "Ten Professors' Declaration," to give a public lecture on "Culture and the Standards for Constructing Culture." A large audience attended, filling the seats. First, Yang Weiyu, the director of the society's office, gave an introductory speech, followed by Mr. He's speech, which lasted for over an hour, elaborating in detail, moving the audience. Mr. He first stated that his speech completely represented the meaning of the ten comrades, but if there were any errors, he would take sole responsibility and hoped that everyone would correct him. Next, he stated that culture is the result of human adaptation to the environment to improve life, which contains the meanings of hard work and continuous progress. In detail, culture is the result of human beings working hard to improve their lives in the face of difficult and challenging environments. The ancients said, "Renewing daily, and again daily, striving for the utmost good," which is what it means. The reason why the ten comrades wanted to publish the "Ten Professors' Declaration" is because they felt that the inherent culture of this country, measured by modern standards, is no longer applicable, while Western culture, measured by Chinese standards, is not suitable, making our ancient civilization, like a flickering lamp, unable to discard the old or create the new, drifting in a state of transition. At the same time, they also saw that China has suffered deeply from the oppression of imperialism in the past century, making our great country suffer from internal hardship and external isolation, and the survival of the nation for more than 4,000 years is in imminent danger. It seems that it is necessary to urgently open up a new path to save the nation. Therefore, they put forward an opinion based on the duty of every citizen and asked the people of the country for guidance. The ten comrades believe that to construct an indigenous Chinese culture, we must neither stick to the old nor blindly follow, and we must first recognize the needs of China at this time and place. The most urgent needs of China now are (1) enriching the people's lives, (2) supporting the survival of society, (3) developing the people's livelihood, and (4) continuing the life of the nation. Therefore, whether it is inherent or foreign culture, we should preserve and introduce everything that meets the above needs, otherwise, we should reject it. Therefore, these four needs are the standards for us to construct an indigenous culture. Mr. He finally concluded that human progress is endless, and the ultimate goal of constructing culture is to create healthy individuals to form a healthy society. As for how to achieve this goal, due to time constraints and because it is not within the scope of the topic, it cannot be elaborated.

Zhou Dingming and Others Initiate Zhou Scholarship Fundraising Association

Membership Limited to Zhou Clan; Intend to Invite Zhou Clan Members from All Locations to Join

Zhou Lingming, a 27th-generation descendant of Song Confucian Zhou Lianxi, a native of Shaoxing, believes in Christianity, and likes public welfare. He once worked hard to restore the Zhou Lianxi Public Ancestral Hall in Hangzhou West Lake, and was highly regarded by his clan for his diligence and was elected as the accounting director, achieving excellent results. In recent years, he has served as a clerk for the China Leprosy Relief Association and Christian educational and charitable organizations in Shanghai, and has been diligent and conscientious in his work. Now, in view of the decline of the Zhou clan and the fact that many of its children are illiterate, he has resolutely invited the clan members of the Zhou Lianxi lineage to prepare for the establishment of a Zhou Scholarship Fundraising Association for impoverished children. All impoverished descendants of the Zhou clan have the right to receive scholarships when they study up to the fourth grade of elementary school, until university. However, this matter is of great importance, and it is not easy to establish. Once the number of participants reaches the statutory number, the predetermined chairman Zhou Wenyu will lead the way and submit an application to the authorities for registration.

Various Sectors in the City Prepare for Anti-Spitting Campaign

Scheduled to Be Held for Four Days Starting on the 28th of This Month; Second Preparatory Meeting Decides on Various Measures Yesterday

The China Tuberculosis Prevention Association, in view of the citizens' habit of spitting everywhere, which is not only harmful to personal health but also affects public health, has specially joined forces with various agencies and organizations in the city to jointly carry out the anti-spitting campaign, starting on the 28th of this month, divided into Student Day, Worker's Day, Merchant Day, and Organization Day for four days. Yesterday afternoon, the second preparatory meeting was held at the association to decide on various measures, which are recorded as follows:

Preparatory Meeting

The attendees were Wang Longzhang from the City Party Headquarters, Qian Fugong from the Municipal Education Bureau, Hu Changzhi from the Health Bureau, Lei Kenan from the Social Affairs Bureau, Xiao Yaxiong from the Public Security Bureau, Deputy Director Duck of the Public Concession Health Department, representative Hertzke Tuo, Yu Zuoting and Zhu Boyuan from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Ye Xiang from the General Labor Union, Xie Yanbo from the Boy Scout Council, Wei Zengpei from the YWCA, Zhang Wei from the Chinese Medical Association, Zhang Junjun, Fan Kanru, Li Zhaozhang, and Liu Minan from the Tuberculosis Prevention Association, etc. Zhang Junjun chaired the meeting, and Fan Kanru recorded the meeting. The important resolutions were: (1) Worker's Day: The General Labor Union will designate several factories to hold ceremonies and distribute statements and paste slogans on Chinese-owned buses and trams. (2) Student Day: The Education Bureau will order schools to hold ceremonies separately and sing the anti-spitting song. The principals of each school will attend and give speeches. All declarations, slogans, and anti-spitting songs will be sent by the association to the Education Bureau for distribution. (3) Merchant Day: The Municipal Chamber of Commerce will distribute declarations, paste slogans on thoroughfares, and order all trade associations to proceed uniformly. (4) Organization Day: The City Party Headquarters is requested to order all organizations to participate uniformly. (5) A letter is sent to the local medical colleges to send personnel to collect street sputum for examination and to analyze the components of tuberculosis bacteria in the sputum. The temporary motions were: (1) The Municipal Education Bureau is requested to order all schools not to mark students absent on the day when their boy scouts participate in the campaign. (2) The Municipal Education Bureau will post slogans at all recreational venues. (3) The association will draft a simple speech and ask the Education Bureau to order all radio stations in the city to broadcast the speech at the scheduled time.

The event is divided into days: First Day, Student Day: (1) Major newspapers publish declarations. (2) The Municipal Education Bureau is requested to order all schools to hold a simple ceremony at 9:00 AM on this morning, sing the anti-spitting campaign song, and the principal of the school will report on the significance of the campaign. From that day on, the school authorities should pay special attention to spitting facilities, or make full use of waste paper (such as newspapers) cut into squares, and hang them everywhere for spitting. Second Day, Worker's Day: (1) The General Labor Union is requested to consult with all employees of important factories in the city to hold a campaign ceremony on this day and paste slogans and distribute leaflets. (2) The Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association is requested to order the worker youth service groups to lead the ceremony at each factory from 6:00 AM this morning. (3) The General Labor Union is requested to broadcast the speech. Third Day, Merchant Day: (1) Print a number of slogans and paste them uniformly on the shops in the prosperous streets of the city on this day. (2) The Municipal Chamber of Commerce is requested to send people to broadcast the speech. Fourth Day, Organization Day: All organizations are requested to promote as much as possible during the campaign period, distribute leaflets, and paste slogans.

"Selection of Yuan Lyrics and Miscellaneous Dramas," Two Books to Be Published

Mr. Wang Junyu Zhang has served as a professor of lyrics and music at various public and private universities in Shanghai for many years. He has a very deep understanding of lyrics and music. His book "The Rules of Yuan Lyrics" has a total of ten volumes and more than one million words. It took him more than ten years to write. He has supplemented and corrected the omissions in the "Selection of Yuan Dramas" in detail, and also explained the errors in the Guangzheng Dacheng and other books. It is a major contribution to lyric and music scholars. The book was formally undertaken by the Shanghai Commercial Press last autumn and will soon be published. In addition, Mr. Wang has compiled a "Selection of Miscellaneous Dramas" in his spare time, which covers various styles of northern and southern dramas. It is indeed an essential book for university music courses. It was also formally undertaken by the publishing house last winter.

Foreign Rice Settlements Quite Active, Margin Gold Drops Then Recovers

Market Conditions Mostly Sideways, Slight Dip of Seven Jiao

Yesterday's gold market saw the price of gold in London plummet, though it recovered later. Initially sluggish, the market was sustained by significant buying due to active foreign rice settlements, leading to a temporary boost in subsequent trading. Silver prices rose consecutively, ultimately stabilizing. According to foreign news, overseas silver markets saw a slight decrease in Britain and remained stable in America. However, sources claimed that America raised prices by 0.125 and India by 0.0625 after the market closed. Forward silver prices saw mixed fluctuations. Exchange rates contracted. London gold prices were severely impacted by the cabinet upheaval, plummeting by one shilling eight and a half pence, shaking confidence. Some retail investors, based on reports of a proposed 100 million yuan financial bond issuance, mistakenly speculated that it implied inflation. Consequently, pre-market trading opened at 71.2 yuan, but retail investors absorbed the initial drop. Large traders repeatedly sold off, breaking the 70 yuan barrier and dropping to 68.9 yuan. The Central Bank's official exchange rate showed stable British rates but contracted American rates, with the customs gold unit plummeting 0.0025 yuan. The margin gold standard was 903 yuan. Prices initially fell in the morning, but strong support emerged, and banks bought at bargain prices, gradually pushing the price back up. Foreign rice settlements were lively, with HSBC and Mercantile Bank actively buying, tightening the domestic market and pushing prices above 70 yuan temporarily. HSBC's official exchange rate revealed stable British rates and a contraction of 0.125 in American rates, with minimal impact. The Central Bank sold shillings, and banks also sold at high prices, gradually pulling prices back within the 70 yuan range. However, the overall trend was very calm, with prices fluctuating only slightly. The foreign exchange market remained stable, but retail investors actively sold off. The market was flat in the afternoon, hovering around 70 yuan, with large traders continuing to provide support. Retail investors were exhausted, and rumors of a 0.034 anna contraction in Indian silver prices stirred up strong buying interest, causing a brief surge. However, large traders took the opportunity to sell off, pushing prices down. Despite Sassoon buying shillings, Indian silver prices rose twice consecutively by one anna, causing prices to fluctuate and eventually decline. However, buyers emerged at lower prices, leading to another period of sideways trading. The day's market remained lackluster with low trading volume. Given the crowded settlement season, the trend is expected to remain stable. Yesterday, both sides posted eight jiao for the forward rate. The following summarizes the day's market conditions.

Morning: Opened at 868.9 yuan, down 4.1 yuan from the previous close. Heng Yu and Ri Chang sold, dropping from 9.3 yuan to 7 yuan. Mercantile Bank bought June shillings at 0.0625, with Da De Cheng, Da Da Chang, Da Yong Li, and Da Fa Yong Ying Xiang buying, pushing prices to 9.2 yuan. Heng Yu sold strips, retreating to 7.7 yuan. Yong Li and Da Fa Yong took strips, pushing prices to 9.5 yuan. Heng Yu, Fu Yu, Fu Xing, and Yong Shang sold, retreating to 7.3 yuan. Fu Yu, Ying Xiang, Heng Yu, Wan Yu, and Hui Xiang took strips, rising to 71 yuan. Heng Yu and Da De Cheng sold strips at high prices, retreating to 69.5 yuan. Mercantile Bank released May US dollars at 0.125. Hui Xiang, Da De Cheng, Heng Yu, Qian Chang Xiang competed to buy, rising to 72.3 yuan. Da Da and retail investors sold at high prices, retreating to 0.06 yuan. Qian Chang Xiang, Yu Qing, Yong Wan Xing continued to push prices to 1.18 yuan. Mercantile Bank released June US dollars at 0.9375, Heng Yu and Fu Yu sold strips, the Central Bank continued to release shillings, and prices fell to 68.7 yuan. Mercantile Bank bought June 38 yuan. Yu Qing, Yong Fu Yu, Wan Xing, Da Da took strips at low prices, recovering to above 70 yuan. Fu Yu and Yi Feng Yong sold slightly, at which time prices hovered around 70 yuan. Securities

The Reason for Bond Market Instability

Increased Margins in the Market

Yesterday, at the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange, due to the approaching settlement date, there was a trend with the potential to continue rising. However, the sudden approval by the Central Political Committee of the 100 million yuan financial bonds, initially considered to have excellent terms and short duration, would not likely cause congestion and affect market stability. It is heard that these bonds are fully collateralized at a 65% discount with the Central, China, and Communications Banks, and the funds are intended to relieve the market. But with such a large amount of cash flowing out, the financial sector inevitably sells other bonds to supplement funds. Abundant market margins are still due to the impact of accepting financial bonds. Furthermore, it is noted that the 22nd series of ten thousand yuan notes, totaling 2,000, can soon be exchanged for thousand-yuan notes, which will further increase market margins by 20 million. All of these factors have dealt an unexpected blow to long positions. Currently, due to the approaching settlement date, there is still some upward pressure, and it is not yet time to be pessimistic. Yesterday's developments: the market price was chaotic during the morning opening. The dismissal of soldiers' bonds for the current month rose by 0.4 yuan, seemingly with some short squeeze action, and the back series also saw some long squeezes. The market price saw both upward and downward trends. In the second session, the 21st series saw some buying, and short-term traders were also active. Market prices increased by 0.2 to 0.3 yuan. The afternoon situation changed slightly. Although the 43rd series still saw some short-term traders, the northern brokers and the 54th series saw significant selling, and the trading floor became looser. Before the opening, there was a firm upward trend, but starting with the salt tax bonds, it was felt that the rally could not be sustained and instead fell by 0.05 to 0.1 yuan to 0.3 yuan. At the close, market sentiment was weak, and selling pressure gradually increased. The impact of financial bonds gradually affected the market, and prices generally weakened, mostly by 0.1 to 0.2 yuan to 0.35 yuan. The current month's 23rd series customs bonds fell sharply by 0.65 yuan. The market price results: the front series saw a few good performances, rising by 0.05 to 0.1 yuan to 0.2 yuan, while the back series mostly fell by 0.05 to 0.1 yuan to 0.55 yuan. Grains: Flour and Wheat Rise Together Due to Spring Snow

— Import Wheat Prices Also Rise Again

Flour: After the market opened in the morning, prices for all months showed a uniform surge. Import wheat quotations from Chicago rose by a significant 7 to 8 jiao, and those from Canada rose by 1 jiao. Upon opening, import wheat quotations rose sharply, and because of sudden weather changes, spring snow was seen in the north, which, according to historical patterns, seemed to have a significant impact on the wheat harvest. Therefore, market sentiment was excited, and buyers were very active. A portion of short positions were also actively covered, causing near-term prices to rise by 0.2 fen and distant-term prices to rise by 0.3 to 0.4 fen. This situation was almost entirely driven by weather concerns. When the market opened in the afternoon, trading for all months was still active, but the trend gradually eased as the weather cleared up and some long positions were unwound, causing prices to fall by nearly 0.1 fen compared to the morning. Looking ahead, weather changes are unpredictable, and with the movement to raise the price of import wheat, there may still be changes in the future. As a result, the current month's price rose by 1.75 li, April's price rose by 0.2 fen, May's price rose by 0.225 fen, June's price rose by 0.3 fen, July's price rose by 0.25 fen, and August's price rose by 0.2 fen.

Wheat: After the market opened in the morning, prices for all months generally showed a stable trend. Import wheat quotations from Chicago rose by varying amounts of 7 to 8 jiao, and those from Canada rose by 2 jiao. When opening, given the rise in import wheat quotations and spring snow in various regions, buying interest in all months was strong, and prices also rose by 0.3 to 0.5 fen. However, due to smooth arrivals of spot import wheat, there were lingering concerns, and the price increase was limited. When the market opened in the afternoon, trading had become quiet, with little activity and little price fluctuation. Given this situation, there is unlikely to be excessive price increases. As a result, July's price rose by 0.3 fen, August's price rose by 0.3 fen, and the current month's price rose by 0.6 fen in the morning. The afternoon session did not open. Spot wheat prices did not trade due to customer quotations.

Cold Weather Causes Simultaneous Improvement in Domestic and Imported Rice

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the arrival of rice from out-of-town merchants was scarce. Only numbers 11 and 12 arrived (a total of just over 2,000 shi). Due to the sudden cold weather, market sentiment turned stable, and sales were quite active. There were bulk purchases of over 1,000 bags each by merchants from Tianjin and Yantai. Consequently, prices for all varieties of thick glutinous rice and lower-grade indica rice stabilized, and the situation was even somewhat tight. Du Jian rice did not see much fluctuation, while Yin Yuan rice weakened by nearly a jiao.

(North Shanghai) Recently, the waterway at Yujidun was blocked for several days due to stone boats running aground, causing a shortage of rice from out-of-town merchants. Although sales in the market were not good, the scarcity of arrivals caused the market price of white glutinous rice to increase by 1 jiao. Bian Yuan and Ke Yuan rice also became tight. Prices for other varieties stabilized, but sales of early-season low-grade indica rice were slow, and prices remained weak.

(Imported Rice) Yesterday, the imported rice market was initially expected to decline as arrivals had been continuous for several days, shaking the confidence of wholesalers. However, after the market opened yesterday morning, the sudden cold weather, which was expected to harm agricultural production, caused market sentiment to turn upwards. Although both arrivals and inventories of spot imported rice were high, local merchants became eager to purchase again, and activity in the interior was even stronger than in Shanghai. Purchases were resumed in Nanjing, providing an opportunity for the market to turn around. Prices for all varieties remained stable only because some traders were seeking to unload their holdings. There were inquiries about futures from both local, inland, and Yangtze River merchants, and new trading was quickly halted. Clearing of inventories led to a price rebound. 500 tons of Saigon long-grain and round-grain rice for March/April delivery were sold, with long-grain rice rising by 0.3 to 0.5 fen and round-grain rice rising by 0.7 to 0.8 fen. The future trend remains firm. Over 12,000 bags of spot rice were traded, mostly purchased by merchants from Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. Inventories of domestic indica rice were low. Over 400 bags of machine-milled red rice and brown rice were purchased from local merchants, and the market was slightly active.

Sugar Market: Another Batch of Zhizhi Foreign White Sugar Put Up For Sale - Price Already Low, Guard Against Future Rebound

Yesterday, the sugar market trend showed signs of flatness and weakness again. The association's quotations for grade 24 white sugar were 16.75 yuan, but no deals were made. Re-exported goods were quoted at 4.72 yuan, a decrease of 0.03 yuan, and some transactions took place. Rough Dutch white sugar for import on the 25th was quoted at 4.68 yuan, and French rough white sugar was quoted at 4.6 yuan, with several hundred bags being traded for each. The local factory's refined white sugar market rebounded slightly, with quotations rising by 0.05 yuan. Chaozhou merchants continued to put up for sale a batch of Zhizhi foreign white sugar, totaling 400 to 500 bags, at a price of 12.5 yuan, with lower grades at discounted prices. According to other merchants, this price was already low, and therefore, those with goods on hand were unwilling to continue selling.

Metals: Tea Merchants Purchase Forward Qing Lead

Tea merchants have recently become interested in Qing lead, leading to considerable trading in recent days. However, overseas prices are rising steadily, and the exchange rate for pound sterling is not improving. Therefore, there is concern that prices will rise again. Tea merchants and factory users are worried about a resurgence of price increases and are therefore rushing to purchase forward contracts. Yesterday's market transactions reached over 2,000 bars, with prices reportedly at 13.75 yuan per dan.

Free Talk

Ordinary Words

— Leng Mo

Science excels at categorization. According to physiology, it is easy to classify a living being as female, male, or other categories. However, general society lacks scientific knowledge, and even with it, it is difficult to say whether social events can be handled using scientific methods. By habit, we feel that there are only two genders. Therefore, when a person enters society, they must be either A or B. Because exceptions are rare in fact, this simple classification is maintained, and no one feels the need to dissent. Because there is no dissent, those born as exceptions are unwilling to speak out. Therefore, the number of exceptions remains unknown, but it is probably more than usually imagined. Perhaps after we know a number, we will no longer be surprised by the occasional exception that must be revealed. We are often surprised by such things, which is unfortunate for us, and even more so for the person and event that are surprised.

In anecdotal novels, there are often records of men turning into women and women turning into men. We don't need to pay attention to the accuracy or degree of accuracy of these records, but the view of these two situations is worth noting. Unfortunately, a man turning into a woman is often seen as a demon or due to karma. As for a woman turning into a man, it is often said that her ancestors had accumulated good karma. Because society's views on these two situations are different, when raising an infant of unclear gender, in order to prevent future misfortune, it is often better to temporarily assume that they are female. This is the best choice for the children. For themselves, the biggest trouble for a woman is that she cannot marry when she grows up and must be supported in old age. If the child is considered a man, there are various troubles or even unexpected dangers related to property and career in the old society. If such an exceptional child raised as a female truly leans towards femininity when they grow up, there is not much of a problem. There are even cases where they marry and the husband's family hides the issue. If they grow up and lean towards masculinity, their misfortune is unavoidable. The very few who are so noticeably masculine that they resemble what is generally considered to be male and formally change to male are, of course, the most fortunate. However, the social psychology that determined their past fate and has not yet disappeared will still cast an embarrassing shadow over them.

Modern thinkers often believe in a kind of spiritual androgyny in their views on gender in the future. This is not a new theory. From the oldest religious figures to the latest scholars, many believe that the restraint of primitive desires helps the achievement of career success. Although many theories state that forced abstinence has many drawbacks, the achievements of many who have lived solitary lives in the past prove that drawbacks are not necessarily inevitable. At least, what is lost is worth what is gained. People with physiological abnormalities naturally also have primitive desires, which often makes people feel that it can lead to an abnormal life. However, if they have hope for development in spiritual life, they must be extremely willing to work hard. Although we may not necessarily hope that their achievements will be above ordinary people, we can conclude that they can be the same as ordinary people and there is no difference. Perhaps there are many achievements of this kind of people in academic and artistic achievements, they are fortunate not to be known, and can enjoy their quiet life and achieve something.

Indeed, today's society is different from the past. The status of women is the same as that of men. A person with physiological abnormalities does not need to worry about their gender as much as before, and there is no need to announce it, which would cause everyone to feel surprised. However, it is difficult to say whether we have actually progressed to this point. And to avoid surprise by not being known, these kinds of things are always regarded as unusual. In fact, physiologists are already familiar with a little physiological peculiarity. Since everything else is as ordinary as ordinary people, we should let them express themselves in society like ordinary people.

Boat Across the Lu River

— Fei Er

The years stuck on the west bank of the Lu River were like flies stuck on candied fruit: my heart was stuck and felt extraordinarily bored, and my nerves were suffocated by the lazy atmosphere of the long-term heat and felt a little itchy. Watching my youth being eroded and the energy of my life being lost from now on. As soon as Mr. Lin proposed a trip to a different place, the stagnant mood became lively and rippled.

So a sampan was placed in the river. Carrying a small suitcase, I jumped joyfully into the river.

The forests on both sides of the Lu River were illuminated by the bright sunlight, and the earth issued a joyful laugh of life. The water of the Lu River flowed to the sea babbling, life is active without stopping. At the bend of the river, the tide stirred up slight gasps, causing eddies. Watching the round-headed fish often stick their heads out to breathe on the surface of the water, and suddenly sink when reflected by the shadow of the paddle. The breath of this world is so difficult, I and the fish have the same feeling in our hearts.

The grass hut of the fishermen on the shore constantly spit out gray-black smoke. When the sampan went along the shore, the aroma of cooked fish and shrimp could often be smelled. Familiar fishermen often greeted, and human life seemed to be filled with warmth. The fishermen's planks stretched long into the riverbed, and loads of fish and shrimp were carried into the huts. A burst of laughter after the harvest hung on the corners of the fishermen's mouths, and labor showed that it had been rewarded.

The boatman was a Malay in his forties. On the boat were his wife and a five- or six-year-old girl. In the boat, the peaceful and sweet conversations within their family often made me yearn for them. The little girl's brown face flushed red, and her lively and innocent attitude was endearing. Mr. Lin kept praising the Malay way of life; if I were not a modern Chinese, I think I would also like to grow up in the coconut groves.

The western sun shone on the muddy red river water, and an umbrella shaded the two of us. The vast river heart often blew in the tropical breeze, and the river water was fanned into circles of ripples.

A tickling sensation crawled across my nerves, and my heart felt a little dazed. The taste of wandering is eternally lauded, and life is like being filled with the taste of bitter and spicy chili peppers, or mellow old wine.

The journey of a few hours in the water took several turns on the Lu River, and the sluggish journey was filled with Malay whispers. Let the slight sweat soak through the white thin clothes; the Malay boatman mysteriously used a small black mole on my collarbone to determine my life's destiny.

Trying to cover up the wounds of life with a smile, I looked at the great natural scenery and stared at the distant and unknown future. Philosophy will be restricted by narrow minds, but sharp eyes can penetrate the clouds and see the blood-red mist of the West.

Although the sky was bright and clear with only a few thin white clouds, and one corner of the west was red, the sun happily followed the clusters of red mist.

In the blink of an eye, the mouth of the Lu River was already visible, and a small, short, gray-black house was already exposed on a prominent spot. Behind it was a small row of houses, shining white in the sun.

A small steamboat had just slowly sailed in from the river mouth, preparing to moor in the heart of the river. The Malay child suddenly shouted out in Chinese from his small mouth:

"The ship is coming! The ship is coming!"

So he clapped his light and thin little hands and jumped on the sampan.

A burst of joy in my heart also hooked me up. The child's cry aroused laughter on the whole boat.

Stepping onto the river bank, the feeling of confusion disappeared completely, and a real image flashed up. Looking at the small journey that had just come to an end, the illusion was like a water splash, crushed by reality, like foam on the water wiped away by the wind.

A Little Compendium of Wandering

— Lin Jia

When the mandolin plays softly,

It matches the rhythm of this head shaking,

Pour a cup of dark red tea,

Listen to who is striding outside the window.

Maybe there will be wind and rain tonight,

Maybe there will be no stars in the sky tomorrow night,

Listen to the softly playing mandolin,

Matching the staggering footsteps outside the window.

The Valley of Miasma (Continued Conclusion)

— Wu Yan

He would always answer like this, but before long, he would start his nagging again, from the demons of miasma to the Baiyi people who could live in it, and how their beautiful women would turn into owls at night to catch people. If it weren't for the constant anxiety in my heart about the miasma, it might have been quite enjoyable to listen and walk along.

Because I was walking fast, he had to hurry to catch up, and soon I couldn't hear him talking, only the sound of his panting. I thought gleefully, "See if you'll still be so talkative!" After walking for a while, he fell behind, and I thought he was going to shout again:

"Wait a minute, don't go so fast!"

To continue the words "She flies at the door latch, like a white butterfly," but he didn't. I turned back curiously to look.

Oh, his face had turned gray and green, large beads of sweat were popping out on his forehead, and thin, clear water was flowing from his nostrils.

"Brother, are you sick?"

I slowed my pace.

"Could it be you've got acute intestinal pain?"

He shook his head and raised his trembling hand to wipe the sweat from his forehead.

"Could it be you've been hit by miasma?"

I looked back in alarm: the sky was darkening, and the valley was exhaling mist.

A figure emerged from the small path in the woods beside the road, startling me.

My traveling companion asked him a question, and he answered, revealing a row of black teeth. Only then did I see clearly that he was carrying a hoe on his shoulder. But I couldn't understand what they were saying, it must have been the Yi language.

While I was still sizing up the back of the black-toothed man, my companion seemed to have regained some of his vitality, nudged my shoulder, and said:

"It's okay, let's go!"

He pulled his sleeve to wipe his nose and forehead, and walked ahead of me with great effort.

"Who was that? A Yi person?"

"Mmm, mmm."

"Hey, I'm asking you! Was that a Yi person?"

"Mmm, yes."

"What did you say to him just now?"

"Mmm, mmm. Don't talk, let's talk at the inn!"

He now seemed to dislike my nagging, quickly cutting off my questions with a rough voice, and quickly quickening his pace.

Thinking about how I had been urging him earlier, and now he was urging me, I couldn't help but smile.

"I thought you were sick just now, judging by this, you could still go to battle!"

He didn't answer, just kept walking.

Turning past the woods, two thatched houses with bamboo walls appeared in the stifling heat and twilight. A pole with children's clothes hanging on it was drying in front of the door.

My traveling companion walked towards the thatched house, saying:

"Let's rest here and then continue on our way, this is a Baiyi family."

Regardless of whether I agreed or not, he lifted the bamboo door and went inside.

I hurried in, complaining to him.

"It's going to be dark soon, why are we still dawdling!"

The house was dark. A bed with an oil lamp lit, casting a faint yellow light, squatted in the corner of the wall. My traveling companion was lying right on it, staring blankly at the opium bubble being roasted on the lamp - it was the Baiyi host sleeping opposite him, roasting it for him.

A woman with a foot-high black turban wrapped around her head let me sit on a bench, and I thought anxiously... Why am I staying here to be a sacrifice to the miasma? Seeing my traveling companion comfortably taking a long puff of opium, I slapped the bench and asked angrily...

"Brother, how can you be so muddleheaded, have you forgotten that the miasma comes out at night?"

He raised his opium pipe and waved it, saying humorously:

"With this gun in my hand, am I still afraid of it?"

I walked out of the house without a word, walking along the dark road and thinking: Traveling with such a Chinese person is truly the unluckiest thing ever.

War Miscellany (8)

— Written by Tokunaga Sunao, Translated by Ye Yin

(III)

My father returned in triumph.

Almost at the same time, my uncle also returned.

Nearby, the adjacent row of houses was celebrating the triumph, it was very lively. My home was also disturbed by the big drums and old sanxian for more than three days.

My father, whom I hadn't seen for two years, was darker and thinner than before. Moreover, he always had an expression as if he were a guest, and was very gentle to us children.

My father, wearing an old black flower gown, sat in the middle of the guests, smiling happily at the gentle villagers. Among the guests, some remarkable people also came. The first was the village head. Although it was only for an hour or so, he said many things to my father, who was apprehensive, before leaving, such as: "You've worked hard..." "Congratulations on your triumphant return." "This is also due to the Emperor's might," and so on. The villagers, who had previously not even bothered to turn their heads, also specially spoke flattering words and came to congratulate him. Huimei's grandfather also came. I was overjoyed.

For about half a year after the war ended, there were various celebrations of triumph. My father would take me along and often bring back bottled wine and food stored in boxes. When the Triumphant Celebration was held in the sacred garden of Kato Kiyomasa, enshrined in Honmyo-ji Temple, I would also follow my father, who had a white copper leaf badge and a military badge hanging in front of him. When women with reddened faces from drinking dressed up as soldiers, dragged long swords with a clatter, and shouted "Banzai! Banzai!" into the banquet hall, the officers stroking their long hair would also smile and hug the women.

One hundred and fifty yuan was issued from above as a reward to my father, who was "Eighth Class Order of Merit, Eighth Class Merit." Since his triumphant return, he hadn't done much odd jobs for others, so he used that money as capital to start driving a freight wagon. My father, who originally didn't have a fixed occupation, learned to lead horses during the war, which enabled him to start that kind of business.

One very lucky night, an old chestnut mare with only one eye was brought over by my grandfather and father, who had been horse traders when they were young. And, they built a shed behind the row of houses and put the horse inside.

Before a year had passed since the war, the very severe recession came. My father, who had started a freight wagon business, had many days when he had nothing to do.

"What freight wagon, it's better not to do it. Every day there's nothing to do, the horse and the people have to eat, how can we maintain it..."

My mother often said these words, questioning my father. Since his triumphant return, his mind seemed to be less clear than before.

"A-Zhi, go and ask if there's any freight to transport today."

Whenever he was questioned by my mother, my father, who was always silent, would call me over and ask me to go to Yicheng Company to ask "if there's any freight."

At Yicheng Company, at the junction of the village end and the township, dozens of white-walled rice warehouses were lined up. When the market was good, the warehouses here were empty, and the rice was moved out of the warehouses. Hundreds of freight wagons lined up, making magnificent shouts, and went back and forth to Kumamoto Station and Kumamoto Station. This Yicheng Company, which held the throat of Higo rice, especially the production areas of Yamaga, Kikuchi, Ozu, and Aso, had a branch office of the Rice Inspection Office and branches of Higo Bank and Hokuto Bank.

Because I went there often, I was very familiar with the situation there. When I came home from school and passed in front of these warehouses, I would often pay attention to see if there was any freight to transport and if my father was there, and I could naturally and indirectly confirm it: this had already become my habit.

Recently, there were very few days when there was freight to transport. However, the state of rice production in the farmers' families had not changed at all. The amount of rice and miscellaneous grains transported out by the farmers, five bags, ten bags, was truly astonishing; even before the harvest, there were often many rice grains being peddled in front of the warehouse store.
