Shen Bao Local Supplement

Conversations

Yao Jinping Turns From Female to Male

— Xia Yun

So That's How It Is – Much Ado About Nothing

The news of Yao Jinping turning from female to male caused a sensation not only in the whole country, but even among Europeans and Americans living in China, such as Mr. Feibai, the Chief of Police of the French Concession, who wanted to see Yao in person as soon as possible. It also aroused deep concern among medical circles. Who knew that after examination by the National Shanghai Medical College on Haig Road, Yao Jinping was still a woman, and there was absolutely no change in her physiology. A mystery was completely cleared up, it was truly ridiculous.

I think the reason why Yao Jinping suddenly had this strange idea and acted so cunningly was entirely because she was eager to go to Xinjiang to find her father, but she was afraid that a female expedition would be inconvenient in many ways, so she had no choice but to do this. But before General Li Du proposed sending her to the National Shanghai Medical College for examination, she would inevitably have to show her true colors when she reached the end of her rope. At that time, she should have told the truth and saved a lot of trouble. However, she did not do so. After the examination, it turned out that that was how it was, and only then did the truth come out. She was truly foolish in the extreme.

Therefore, I think there are many things in the world that can be viewed in this way. Unless you see them with your own eyes, all strange rumors are not to be believed. However, although Yao Jinping's actions were said to be out of filial piety and for the convenience of a distant expedition, she had no choice but to do this. But in ancient times, women disguised as men, either to find their husbands or to fight in battles, secretly disguised themselves, and privately investigated. This kind of situation was originally a common occurrence in our country's novels. Why did Yao Jinping exaggerate her words and cause a national sensation? This is also something that cannot be measured by reason.

Moreover, recently, the strange things reported in the newspapers have been emerging one after another. For example, in Hongkou Lane Hongqiao, a large rat ran under the God of Wealth, and the God of Wealth Temple suddenly collapsed. Last year, at the Great East Gate of Shanghai, a large snake fell from the sky due to lightning. Also, a human-faced spider was found in a civilian's house in Madian, Hankou. And, a sleeping beauty was discovered in a certain country, who slept for two years and nine months. These are all strange news that cannot be verified. But Yao Jinping, although a woman, was the subject of many rumors, and most people paid attention to her, so that General Li Du was also driven by curiosity to send her to the hospital for examination. Who knew that the magic trick was not real and was immediately exposed in court? This was something that not only General Li Du did not expect, but also something that Yao Jinping did not expect.

Yao Jinping's purpose in turning from female to male was only out of a filial heart to go on a distant expedition to find her father. In this way, her plan to find her father completely failed. But I think that as a result, she may be able to achieve her goal of finding her father. Assuming that her father is still alive, someone will definitely tell her father about this matter, and her father will naturally send a letter to inform her of his current address. Then Yao Jinping will not have to look for her father anymore, and her father will find her. In this way, Yao Jinping's actions are more effective than a full-page advertisement for a year, and this is also something that Yao Jinping did not originally expect.

Old Residence

— Luo Han

In the blink of an eye, it has been a year since the past events. Jing was still studying at the K Girls' School in the northern suburbs of Shanghai at that time, and I also lived with her in a small village near the school for economic reasons.

A winding blue water river surrounds it, with many cargo ships floating on the river. All around are endless green fields, dense green forests, and when the reddish-brown Songhu mini-train passes by, a cloud-like white smoke fills the treetops and is blown away by the wind, like a lively silver dragon.

In the ancient temple in the west of the village, every time the setting sun shines, a deep and long bell sound is emitted, crowding with Roman

Page 18

ancient style.

Our residence was in a south-facing black house along the river. The architecture was a combination of Chinese and Western styles, surrounded by low bamboo fences, which were covered with various kinds of rose flowers. In front of the door was a vegetable garden of about two acres, planted with seasonal vegetables, interspersed with a little red and green wildflowers. When you opened the French window, a gentle breeze blew in the fragrant aroma of wildflowers.

The landlord was a very kind old lady. Her husband had passed away early, leaving behind a son and two daughters, who made a living on a small inheritance. From her mottled gray hair and wrinkled face, you could tell that she had tasted some of the bitterness of life.

Her two daughters were both married, and her youngest son was still studying in middle school, so the house was particularly deserted. At the same time, because of the desolation, it increased her old man's goodwill towards us. She worshiped the Buddha and spent a lot of time chanting scriptures and worshiping Buddha every day. However, she also often came to talk to us, telling us many stories she had experienced when she was young. She told us in detail about the Taiping Rebellion.

Naturally, we were very satisfied with such a landlord and the quiet environment. At that time, we were really happy. Jing went out to study every day, and I went out to work every day. When we were free after work, we would lead a group of neighboring children to play various interesting games, teach them to sing, teach them to dance, and sometimes buy a lot of fruit and eat with them. Or, when the sun went down, we would hold hands and go to the sentry post outside the door to see the crimson setting sun, slowly passing through the brown-colored rosy clouds, sinking into the western mountains. Listening to the deep and long bell sound from the ancient temple, we forgot all our sorrows, we forgot all the troubles and trivial matters in the world.

But good times don't last long, and smoke and clouds are easy to disperse. The petals of the roses were blown off by the bleak autumn wind, and when the autumn insects began to wail, Jing finally left Shanghai for something and separated from me. With a lonely heart, after Pin left, I also moved from that quiet place to Shanghai.

Now it is spring again. By an unexpected chance, I passed by the old residence that I had been away from for a long time. The winding river, the endless green fields, the dense green forests, the black house surrounded by low bamboo fences, the green lawn, the warm spring breeze, welcomed the landlord's kind smiling face, and a group of naive children. Everything, the scene is still the same. The old residence is still there, but unfortunately, the old friend is no longer in front of me.

Murder Case

— Ming

The news of Jin Ge Sao's suicide by hanging reached Dongcun around lunchtime.

Her brother, Fu Cai, was a brainless man. He saw his sister return to Ning, and only after his parents repeatedly persuaded her did she return to her husband's home with eyes swollen like walnuts from crying. Now, when he heard that his sister had committed suicide by hanging, he threw his rice bowl a zhang away and grabbed the hoe in the corner of the room to avenge his sister.

The messenger was Chu Fu Cai's eldest sister's husband, who lived in Xicun with Jin Ge's family. He had learned the news of his wife's sister's suicide early in the morning, but Jin Ge's mother tried her best to hide it. This old woman was known throughout the village as a shrew. Everyone guessed that there would be discord between the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law after Jin Ge got married; even Jin Ge'er, whom this old woman loved like a treasure, was scolded and beaten every day, on the grounds that he had a wife and no mother. According to the rumors in Xicun, the young couple got along very well, and Jin Ge'er was still very considerate to his mother and always advised his wife to be patient. This time, when Jin Ge Sao returned to Ning, the old woman slapped her daughter-in-law for no reason, saying that she was stealing men in her parents' home. When her son tried to persuade her, he was bitten twice on the arm. In the morning, Jin Ge Sao hanged herself in the woodshed.

The old woman, seeing that she had caused a great disaster, forced her son to bury his wife and pretended to go to his wife's family to welcome her back, so as to shift the responsibility to her parents' home. But Jin Ge'er couldn't bear it, and the mother and son quarreled, revealing the matter.

Fu Cai's eldest sister's husband traveled more than ten miles to Dongcun to deliver the news. Seeing that Fu Cai was angry, he quickly grabbed his brother-in-law's hand and said, "Let's discuss it properly."

The result was that the whole family went to Xicun to reason.

The mouths in the countryside are as swift as the wind. Jin Ge's house was surrounded by many people, and in the chaotic voices, you could hear the loud voice of "Damn old woman!" from afar, but no one stood up to resolve this murder case, always maintaining this disturbance.

When Jin Ge Sao's family arrived, the crowd shouted even louder, "Kill the old woman!" and tightened their encirclement.

Fu Cai was the first to rush into the house, like a wild bull freed from its tether, grabbing the old woman and beating her. This was a good show that the audience was hoping for. Although his parents and eldest sister's husband tried their best to pull him away, the enthusiastic family voice was booming like spring thunder, and naturally there were some cheers.

The old woman lay on the ground and refused to get up, her hair disheveled, crying loudly as if her husband had died: "You hit people... good... I'll sue the official!"

Jin Ge'er stood blankly by his wife's corpse, his head down. He did not see this lively scene that was almost like watching a village opera. He looked at his wife's pale face, torn by conflicting justice. However, the old woman cried more and more fiercely, like a mad dog, and the people from Jin Ge Sao's family joined the crowd of onlookers, not knowing what to do.

This tragicomedy cried and quarreled until the sun set in the west, when a village head with high shoulders pushed his way into the crowd. He used his official language to drive away the idlers and took the people involved to the police station.

This is a real event that I personally experienced in a certain village. The result is something that can never be believed: "Acquittal"—on both sides.

— Written by Zhu Yanghui

"Sir, please save him, I only have this one child!"

Xiling Gorge

— Bing Bai

When the boat passed Nanjin Pass in Yichang, it seemed to have entered another world. The mountains on both sides gradually became narrow and narrow, and the river water was no longer as calm as before. One wave chased after another, rushing and roaring; and the small wooden boat we were sitting on was like a clumsy pig, swaying uncertainly in the heart of the river. Fortunately, we were here to visit Xiling Gorge, not to rush on our way for important matters. Otherwise, seeing the boat's clumsy appearance, it would really be infuriating.

The mountains here seem to be competing with the sky, one higher than the other; inserted into the clouds, sometimes, you can't see the top of the mountain at all from the boat. The mountain peaks are piled with white clouds, and people can't see clearly whether it is white clouds or mountain peaks. It is now March, and in Jiangnan, it is already the season of miscellaneous flowers and trees; however, here, the wind is roaring in the gorge, as if it is still the severe winter; what the eyes see is nothing else, in front is the mountain, behind is the mountain, left is also the mountain, right is also the mountain, even the vast sky is blocked by the mountain, only revealing half a face to give us a wry smile; we are groping forward in the land of mountains.

"What, is it going to be dark? The sun has already set." I asked the boatman strangely.

"Sir, it's still early, the sun is blocked by the top of the mountain." The boatman answered me with a smile; I then knew that what the Commentary on the Water Classic said about the Three Gorges, "Without stopping at noon or midnight, you can't see the bright moon," was not lying. People in other places see the sun for twelve hours every day, but here, the sun can only stay for two or three hours, which is also a very interesting life.

The boat barely turned a bend and was still surrounded by mountains. Looking ahead, it seemed that there was no way out. Looking behind, it seemed that there was no way back: where did we come from, where are we going? Li Bai said: "The water of the Yellow River comes from the sky." In this situation, it can also be said that the water of the Yangtze River comes from the mountains. If water were not a flowing thing, the mountain would really swallow the water; what's the point of just looking at the mountains, I grumbled; really, it's so stiff and lifeless; I regret coming this time.

"Sir: don't look at the foot of the mountain, look at the top of the mountain, there are many interesting things on the mountain peaks!" The boatman still said to me with a smile; so, he pointed me out, this is the Beauty Peak, this is the Widow's Cliff, I looked along his direction, and it turned out that the mountain is also the same as a woman, her beauty is on her head, not at her feet.

On the mountain peaks, just talking about her form, there are thousands of changes, some are like tropical beasts, some are like giants in fairy tales, some are beautiful women with open arms waiting to be embraced, some are young women with their heads down lamenting; like pens like knives, like beasts like people, the mountain peaks are just like the ever-changing white clouds, this mountain peak is different from that mountain peak. The withered pine hangs in the middle of the cliff, with her own style of standing proudly alone, the mountain birds coming and going by the river and mountains also have their own pleasure; wildflowers are blooming, and miscellaneous trees are growing densely. The strangest thing is that the monkeys on the mountain cover their ears when they hear the whistle of the steamboat and hide in the crevices of the rocks. If it is the small wooden boat we are riding, no matter how you threaten or scold it, it will ignore you. According to the boatman, there used to be more monkeys in the past, but now they are gradually decreasing year by year.

"What, are those people on top?" I suddenly saw a few people wriggling in the middle of the cliff. That is a cliff as sharp as a knife, and below is the turbulent Yangtze River. If you are not careful and jump down, your corpse will be gone.

"They are cutting grass on top, to make a living, there is no other way, they are all used to it, they wear nailed shoes on their feet, and it is rare to fall down." The boatman explained, and I thought, man is really an unfortunate creature, for the sake of living, they are willing to take any risks.

That night, we stayed in Nantuo, and tomorrow, we will pass the most dangerous Xintan in Xiling Gorge.

The Home of Marble

— Jingfu

In the summers of Lingnan, the elegant ancestral hall doors in my hometown faced the refreshing southern breeze. Children loved to place their nimble feet on the two marble stones beside the door. The smooth, cool marble felt so comfortable, it was as if their bones had softened! In those childhood days, I would squint my little eyes, wondering if the marble came from a foreign country. It was said to be produced in Dali, but I couldn't quite grasp where Dali was!

Dali had always been vague and distant. But once I saw Dali, it was like waking from a long, beautiful dream, so enchanting was the landscape!

The snow-capped Cangshan Mountains, the moon reflected on Erhai Lake, the flowers of Shangguan, the winds of Xiaguan, this is the exquisitely wonderful home of marble!

The towering Cangshan Mountains seem to isolate Dali from the outside world. Facing Erhai Lake in front, gazing at the azure waves of Erhai, one feels as if smiling at a heavenly mirror. Surrounded by vast and serene green mountains and lively, gentle green waters, the air is clear and pure. Cangshan and Erhai embrace each other, encircling Dali in a shape like a fish's belly.

The snow on Cangshan has earned it the nickname "Silver Cang." The weather in Dali is not cold; it's like spring all year round. However, Cangshan is covered with thick snow year-round, never experiencing a day without clouds. The snow is as white as silver, oh, what a silver mountain! The people of Dali live year-round in this embrace of clear air. With the snow as white as silver, the foothills of Cangshan lush and green, and the Erhai Lake as clear as a mirror, its vastness, freedom, and serenity make one yearn for it all the more in these smog-filled civilized cities.

From beginning to end, Cangshan Mountain is densely connected with nineteen magnificent and elegant peaks, with eighteen streams nestled between them, each boasting countless scenic wonders. The mountain's terrain is solid, the rocks treacherous, and the thick, year-round snow accumulates on the mountains. Streams and waterfalls flow freely everywhere. There is no way to climb Cangshan and cross over its summit from behind Cangshan outside of Dali! Nor can one descend Cangshan from the summit on the front side. Similarly, there is no path to reach the summit from the foothills of Cangshan within Dali. But ingeniously, from the head to the tail of Cangshan, there is a flat top like a huge road, directly connecting the entire mountain, preventing people from going up or down, but allowing them to travel from end to end, enjoying the scenery, a vista more exquisite than anything man-made!

In the middle of the wondrously high and dangerous Cangshan Mountains, a band of white clouds hovers, like a white jade belt, a beautiful sight from afar, which the people of Dali call "Jade Belt Locking Cangshan." Airy and ethereal, the people under Cangshan must truly feel a bit like immortals! They might even be willing to plunge into the beautiful waves of Erhai Lake before them, to wash away the dirt and dust from their bodies!

The sea and mountains embrace Dali tightly, seemingly leaving no way through, but precisely where the sea and mountains meet, there is a narrow passage like a winding path, gently leading, as if drifting into a dream, into the welcoming embrace of Dali, like a suddenly opening Peach Blossom Spring!

Approaching the side of Dali, Cangshan is in front. Right at the entrance, Shangguan, there is the Nine Bend Bridge, and at the exit, Xiaguan, there is the Black Dragon Bridge. Crossing the Nine Bend Bridge, a mountain slope rises diagonally, like a ladder. One can only walk in from here, reaching the top of the slope, and then suddenly slip into the mouth of Dali.

Amateur Mailbox

Introducing Some "Handwritten Characters"

Editor:

"Handwritten characters" are undoubtedly much simpler than standard characters. In the past, when writing important documents, one had to write each stroke very carefully and correctly. For example, when writing the words "灑掃" (sǎ sǎo, to sweep and clean), one had to write them in their complex forms, "灑掃," and could not write them as "洒扫." At that time, although we knew that "灑掃" and "洒扫" were the same, we dared not simplify, because people said that these simplified characters were not formal and could not be presented "in polite society." Now it's different. These "not formal" handwritten characters, through the promotion of the government and general literati, have attracted a lot of attention, and three hundred handwritten characters have already been cast into lead type, and a few new magazines have adopted them. I think there are many benefits to these handwritten characters. First, they save time, and they are also easy to learn and write, which is of great help in promoting cultural work. I hope that all newspapers and books will use them as much as possible.

Yesterday, Mr. said that readers could write out the handwritten characters they know that have not been included in the three hundred characters and publish them in the mailbox for reference by those who promote handwritten characters, so I am writing down the characters I know and often use. If there are any mistakes, I hope everyone will correct them. Respectfully,

Wei Zhi

Original Character 閒門觀衆鋼勸

Handwritten Character 　　門觀众鋼劝

Original Character 續廣還體霽墊

Handwritten Character 续泛还体　墊

Original Character 陸喫　幫論無

Handwritten Character 陆吃皱帮論旡

Original Character 應為

Handwritten Character 应為抬

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

The Life of Maureen O'Sullivan We Should Know

— Yi Ji

Maureen O'Sullivan, the couple in "Tarzan the Ape Man," her healthy physique, beautiful face, and natural and lively performance have long been firmly etched in our minds. Not long ago, she also played an innocent young sister in "A Family Affair," adding a lot of color to the film. The three main actors of "A Family Affair," Norma Shearer, Frederic March, and Charles Laughton, are all winners of Hollywood's artistic gold medals and are among the best in the American film industry, but Maureen O'Sullivan's relaxed and natural performance almost surpassed them. But what do we know about her? This is what the reporter wants to tell everyone.

The reason we should get to know her sooner is that she doesn't want to spend her life in the film industry. Her coming to Hollywood is of an "amateur" nature. She wants to marry and have children. These may soon become facts, preventing us from seeing her acting on the screen again. Maureen O'Sullivan has never relied on publicity agents to gain fame. In America, it is because her performance is outstanding that the audience wants to know everything about her. We also want to know her automatically.

Maureen is the eldest of a family of five. Her father is a retired British army officer. She was born in Dublin, Ireland, so she is Irish. When she was eleven years old, her father sent her to a monastery in London to study. Before she was sixteen, she was expelled from the school. The reason for her expulsion was "disobeying teachers and refusing to repent despite repeated warnings." Maureen said, "A student with such a title, which other school would dare to take me in?" Therefore, she broke away from school life.

Soon she went to Versailles, France, to study, because that was a necessary course for fashionable British children. She was in France for only six months before returning to her home in Ireland, playing carefree. Her playmates were all children of military officers. At that time, she never dreamed of being involved in the film industry. She might have married a young military officer and that would have been the end of it. Unexpectedly, Hollywood stretched out its arms and snatched her away.

At that time, the famous director Frank Borzage of Fox Film Corporation was filming John McCormack's Song of My Heart in the Irish capital. One evening, this film crew accidentally stepped into a dance hall. Among hundreds of happy men and women, Frank Borzage suddenly saw Maureen and paid great attention to her. He wrote a note, instructed the waiter to deliver it to her, and asked to talk to her. Maureen heard that this famous American director wanted to talk to her, and she was moved and nodded in agreement. Frank Borzage then ran over and told her that he was looking for a female lead, and she was exactly the person he was looking for.

Maureen knew that her family would definitely oppose her making movies. Therefore, she did not tell her family, but went to the place where Frank Borzage worked every day to watch them filming. She did this for four consecutive days. On the last day of the fourth day, Frank Borzage called her over, put makeup on her, taught her a few lines, and pushed her in front of the camera to start the audition. Maureen felt inexplicable, but she was a talented actress, and the results of the audition were surprisingly good. The next day, Frank Borzage ran to her home and negotiated with her parents. As a result, her mother agreed to accompany her daughter to Hollywood. This was the beginning of Maureen O'Sullivan's arrival in Hollywood, when she was only eighteen years old.

After everything was settled in Hollywood, her mother returned home satisfied. Because Fox Film Corporation did not reuse her, she was signed by MGM after filming a few ordinary films. In addition to being recognized by people for the first time in "Tarzan the Ape Man" and becoming famous in "A Family Affair," she also played the role of David's wife, Dora, in Charles Dickens' famous book "David Copperfield." But although she enjoyed the status of a star, she had a very indifferent view of the film industry or Hollywood. She always maintained her amateur and non-professional attitude.

"Acting"? She said, "I don't feel particularly interested. I am naturally lazy and don't like this heavy work. My fame is entirely due to luck. I have no ambition to be in the film industry, nor do I have any ambition. I am not saying this because I am not grateful, but I always feel that being at home is more happier and freer. Only two things forced me to move forward: one is to accumulate money so that I can be economically independent in the future; the other is vanity, which makes me want to achieve something after I have been in Hollywood for three or four years."

That's right, Maureen doesn't have much money, and she is too lazy, but she will definitely be able to get her wish in the future. As for her achievements, they are already quite impressive. She is only twenty-two years old now.

Review of "Beauty's Heart"

— Hua Lun

——New Light Cinema——

"Beauty's Heart," originally titled "Changbai Mountains and Heilongjiang," is showing this year, which quite reminds us of a page of cartoons between the Changbai Mountains and Heilongjiang. Although this cartoon is made like a mirror covered with sand and dust due to the pressure of certain social customs, this mirror still reflects some faces of those who recognize thieves as fathers and the postures of the large group of people struggling for survival. Therefore, "Beauty's Heart" should receive a higher valuation in the original intention of grasping the theme.

Unfortunately, due to the author's lack of seriousness in the recognition and performance attitude of his own caught great subject, it reduced its due achievement. Naturally, we do not necessarily disagree with the author's use of something like quinine with a sugar coating, such as the "Beauty's Heart" wearing a love romance coat, given the difficulties encountered in some current works that reflect reality, but quinine with an overly thick sugar coating will become sweet candy, just as "Beauty's Heart" has, because the romance coat is too thick, giving people the impression of admiring it as a hero in distress, a young lady rescuing him, and then a happy ending, these old clichés, and ignoring the opposite side, also causing the author to suffer unexpected losses, so-called counterproductive effect. This is a technical problem of expression, and it is also a problem of the attitude of recognition and handling of this issue. Due to the lack of technical expression, Li Duo is written without personality and becomes a mythologized figure. There are no appropriate reasons and arrangements for Su Ru's selfish love for him and her father's sympathy for him. As for the peasant couple, as soon as they heard that he was a "fugitive," they merely said he was a "fugitive" and wholeheartedly regarded him as a national hero, which is too hasty. Due to the lack of understanding of the difficult and painful national tragedy of this nation's resistance against the enemy, the attitude of handling it is inevitably not serious enough. Also, Su Ru carried Li Feng's photo on her maid's body and moved into her home at once. In this family where traitors of the type who recognize thieves as fathers often came, she actually openly rode in and out on horseback and was able to talk love in the back garden, etc. This ignores the serious oppression of the country-destroying people who are densely covered with scouts and strict inspections, and thus weakens the dramatic and touching effect. As for the person who is a consultant of a certain country, these are all very meticulous people, but they would say secrets to some military officers and Han Jian in front of irrelevant old men. Similarly, the commander's office and reception room would be combined into one place, allowing Su Ru to see him stamping important official documents, etc., which is too theatrical! In addition, the part where the Han uncle and nephew gave gifts to Su Ru at the same time is also inconsistent with the identity of the commander Han Jian and Su Ru. Naturally, these are still small details. Let's give another example. When Li Feng and his army, who were seeking welfare for the people, came to fight, the author called Mo Zhi to order the soldiers to revolt. On the screen, the revolt was successful, but in fact, such opportunistic people would never exist in the competition of life and death, right?

From the entire performance point of view, "Beauty's Heart" has mediocre achievements. However, the director inevitably has regrets about taking care of one thing while losing sight of the other when encountering two aspects of depiction. Often, one side is a long paragraph, and the other side is another start, which cannot be intertwined multiplicatively, making the book more lively. The light is more astringent than bright.

Xu Xinyuan and Hu Die are the best in acting skills.

Review of "A Generation of Heroes"

— Ling He

Jew Suss—Cathay

First, I must state that I have not read the original novel of "Jew Suss," so I can only base my criticism on what is shown on the screen. Like "The House of Rothschild" starring George Arliss and "The Wandering Jew" starring Conrad Veidt, it uses the painful and tragic experiences of the stateless Jewish people as the theme of the film. Precisely because the Jews have no country, and precisely because they have suffered the pain of national subjugation, films with a sense of justice reflect their lives and the common hatred of the Jewish people in film. This not only has great artistic value, but more importantly, it has great significance in promoting the spirit of resistance of oppressed nations.

The Joseph Süss presented here may be seen by some as a fool. Such individualistic heroic resistance, viewed from the perspective of the current stage of weak national revolutionary movements, cannot but be considered a mistake in action. However, the author's resentment towards national subjugation, which is entrusted in him, as well as the discrimination and cruel mistreatment they suffered from the Germanic people, in any case aroused the enthusiastic sympathy of the audience. Moreover, this hero bravely sacrificed himself for his nation. In this respect alone, compared with the oppression suffered by the Chinese nation from imperialism, and the pain we have experienced under the iron heel of imperialism, it undoubtedly gives us great stimulation. Therefore, it is very meaningful that this film is shown in China.

"A Generation of Heroes" is a successful work of art. Due to the seriousness of the content, the director, Lothar Mendes, expresses it in a very heavy tone. The playwright's grasp of the script is extremely successful; there are no tasteless transition scenes, only dramatic developments. The director's successful creation of a heavy atmosphere allows every audience member to feel "a heavy oppression of breathing," which is something people dare not ignore.

Of course, this film would not have achieved such success without Conrad Veidt's magical performance. Due to the director's very skillful handling, several scenes are truly surprisingly successful. For example, when Süss returns to his mother's old home, there is a boiling cheer outside, and he embraces his mother with fervent, pure love. He speaks to his compatriots from the window, and the mother and son are intoxicated by the glory of the nation. Until he sees his mother's love letter and learns that he is of German blood, which causes him to show his wavering national consciousness to his revered uncle. His inner pain and contradiction reach the highest level of success. Also, when he learns of his daughter's tragic death, he uncovers the white cloth on the corpse, and he falls heavily beside the body. That silent grief, until he shouts "Long live the Jews!" in front of the door, the process from grief to frenzy, gives people great emotion.

In addition, when he makes Karl die of anger, his gnashing of teeth and curses in Karl's ear, as well as his final moments before execution, are the highest expressions of his acting skills. As for Frank Vospar, who plays Karl, although he also achieves a lot, he is a bit over the top. Everyone else is very dutiful.

In short, this is a successful work.

Movie Novel

India's National Hatred (Cave Of India) (7)

— Mao De

In a little while, that person was already standing in front of her. He looked at her silently and motionless for a long time, then took a step forward and shouted in a very urgent voice: "You are Margaret... yes...; you are Margaret." At this time, he felt that she was the person he had been thinking about in his dreams. But she was even more beautiful than he had imagined in his dreams. Margaret murmured, "The welcome party... the governor..." She tried her best to maintain her composure. Clive asked again: "Let them wait a while. You just tell me... you came here to marry me, didn't you? Please tell me. Of course it is, isn't it?" He was very sure that there was no other answer except yes.

Margaret tried her best to say "no" to maintain her shaky girlish dignity, but when she opened her mouth, she only said a "yes", and stammered with the addition of "that's right." After a while, she suddenly turned her head and shouted, "Oh, no!" Clive couldn't help shouting wildly, "Oh, nothing could be better!" She was the only good woman in his eyes! Margaret also said: "But! You don't know, it's not like before now." Clive thought for a while and said: "Are you talking about me? I really shouldn't have run in to see you in this state: I'm covered in dust and dirt..." Margaret took another step closer and said: "No, no. I said... you are a big man now - you have conquered all of India." Clive laughed and said: "This is just the beginning! In the future, you will also build a big house in Berkeley Square... and high carriages and horses... and one day you will be a duchess!"

Margaret smiled and said: "Is there nothing else besides that?" Clive suddenly said respectfully: "There's also my person, if it's worth you wanting." Margaret said: "Just your person is enough." He grabbed her hand. Suddenly remembering the dirt on his body, he hurriedly apologized: "I'm sorry, my hands, my clothes, are not worthy of touching you." Margaret looked at him for a while, and felt that he was a man of his word, and her heart silently agreed. She took a step forward and kissed him on the lips.

Clive couldn't help shouting after being kissed by her, "Ah, she is truly a brave woman. Okay, let's go. Let's go to the welcome party together. Isn't this a good start?" Margaret said: "Start?" Clive said: "That's right, the start of our life together." Margaret said: "I hope that the ending, when it comes, will be just like this."

They arrived at the meeting place and walked towards the platform where the governor was sitting, amidst the cheers of the crowd. Clive was as high as a person, and Margaret's attitude was very calm, although the hand she had on his arm was trembling slightly. The governor stood up very kindly to welcome them when he saw them approaching. Clive then introduced Margaret. He said she was his future wife. Margaret hurriedly bowed to the governor, and also thanked the public one by one for their salutes.

Finally, they returned to their hometown of England as a couple. They lived in a beautiful house in Queen Square. They were already rich and noble.

But Clive was thinking about a greater and more glorious future. Although according to Margaret's original intention, it would be enough if she and her husband could live together in a small cottage forever, Clive felt that while children are affectionate, heroes are not short of breath. He was determined to conquer the world for the beauty and place it at her feet, so as to win her admiration, joy, and heart. (To be continued)
